131344 7UUUU
131694 RSRC
131701 LVINLBVWd
131719 6Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Listener.  If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
132034 Termination mode specifies how the GPIB driver should determine when the read is finished.  All values from 0-255 (0x0-0xFF) will be taken to be an eos byte which wll stop the read when it is recieved in the data stream or when end is detected.  STOPend 256 (0x100) (the default) indicates to stop the read when end is detected.  The read  will always stop when the requested count has been read.
132434 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
132618 GPIB status vector:
132639 status[0] - Device Clear State
132670  status[1] - Device Trigger State
132704  status[2] - Listener Active State
132740 status[3] - Talker Active State
132773 status[4] - Attention line asserted
132810 status[5] -
132822 Controller In Charge
132843  status[6] - Remote State
132869  status[7] - Lockout State
132897 status[8] - I/O Completed 
132925 status[9] - not used
132946  status[10]- not used
132968  status[11]- not used
132991 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
133031 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
133063  status[14]- Timeout occured
133092  status[15]- GPIB error detected
133128 GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
133181 GPIB Error:
133198 -No error
133213 -Function requires GPIB to be CIC
133252 -No listeners detected on write
133289 -Controller not addressed correctly
133330 -Invalid argument(s)
133357 (perhaps bad address string????)
133395 -Function requires GPIB to be SC
133433 -I/O operation aborted
133461 -hardware not present

191057 GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.

191128 -No error
191143 -Function requires GPIB to be CIC

191697 -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
191789 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
191973 GPIB status vector:
191994 status[0] - Device Clear State
192025  status[1] - Device Trigger State
192059  status[2] - Listener Active State
192095 status[3] - Talker Active State
192128 status[4] - Attention line asserted
192165 status[5] -
192177 Controller In Charge
192198  status[6] - Remote State
192224  status[7] - Lockout State
192252 status[8] - I/O Completed 
192280 status[9] - not used
192301  status[10]- not used
192323  status[11]- not used
192346 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
192386 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
192418  status[14]- Timeout occured
192447  status[15]- GPIB error detected
192481 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.
192734 3Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Talker. If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
193044 The end of transfer mode describes the method of signaling the end of the data to the listener.  Its values are:
193157   2 (default) DABend - Send eoi with last byte.
193205  1 NL end - Send linefeed with eoi after data.
193252  0 NULLend - Do nothing at end of transfer.OKdata string contains the data bytes that the VI sends to the GPIB device.

297513 Instr Error Out Cluster.ctl
297551 status

297581 error out
297731 Instr Error Out Cluster.ctl
298703 ,wwww
299312 RSRC
299319 LVCCLBVW*
299338 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
299683      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
299735      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.

An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
398459 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
398717      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
398768      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
398815      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
398873      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
398930      error, and a positive value is a warning.
398978      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
399025      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
399074 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI."
399166 no error
399175 ERROR
399181 no error
399190 ERROR
399199 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
399544      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
399596      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
399654      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
399711      error, and a positive value is a warning.
399759      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
399809      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
399860 (ABC) 
399867 The name of the VI that is calling this VI.  If an error occurs during the operation of this VI, the value in source will be placed in the source element of the error out cluster. 
400049 (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.

450601 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
450859      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
450910      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
450957      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
451015      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
451072      error, and a positive value is a warning.
451120      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
451167      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
451216 ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
451308 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
451653      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
451705      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
451763      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
451820      error, and a positive value is a warning.
451868      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
451918      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.

481990 /Primary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the low order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions.  The value of 31 (default) means return the NOADDR constant (0xFFFF) as the packed address.  The VI places primary address in the lower byte of the packed address.
482298 Secondary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the high order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions. The value of 31 (default) means use no secondary address. The VI places secondary address in the upper byte of the packed address.
482574 VThis integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  packed address contains primary address in its lower byte and secondary address in its upper byte. You can use packed address as the address input to the GPIB 488.2 VIs. 
482919 True if either primary or secondary addresses are outside ot the range 0-31.  address error indicates whether a range error has occurred.

527029 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
527281 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
527626      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
527678      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
527736      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
527793      error, and a positive value is a warning.
527841      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
527891      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.

638242 Initializes the software connection to the instrument.  In the case of VXI instruments controlled via NI-VXI, initializes the NI-VXI library, reads in the resource manager table, calculates A16 configuration addresses, determines memory requirements, and stores base addresses into A24 or A32 space.  For VXI instruments controlled via GPIB-VXI, performs all of the above except initialization of NI-VXI libraries.  You must run the INSTR Close VI once for every time you run this VI.$

678472 (I32) 
678479 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
678731 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
679076      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
679128      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
679186      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
679243      error, and a positive value is a warning.
679291      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
679341      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
679390 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred."
679529 no error
679538 ERROR
679544 no error
679553 ERROR
679560 (ABC) 
679567 The name of the VI that is calling this VI.  If an error occurs during the operation of this VI, the value in source will be placed in the source element of the error out cluster. 
679750 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
680008      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
680059      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
680106      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
680164      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
680221      error, and a positive value is a warning.
680269      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
680316      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
680365 ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing."

788183 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
788528      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
788580      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
788638      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
788695      error, and a positive value is a warning.
788743      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
788793      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
788842 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
788982 (ABC) Uniquely identifies the instrument to establish communications with.  The grammar for the instrument descriptor is shown below.  Parameters are shown in lower-case and optional parameters are shown in square brackets ([]).
789212 GPIB:   INSTR{GPIB[bd]::prim addr[::sec addr]}
789259 VXI:  INSTR{VXI::logical addr}
789290 GPIB-VXI:   INSTR{GPIB-VXI[bd]::logical addr[prim addr]}
789348 Optional Parameter Default Values:
789383     bd - GPIB board (0)
789407     prim addr - GPIB primary address (1)
789448     sec addr - GPIB secondary address (none)
789493     logical addr - VXI logical address 
789534 EXAMPLE:  A GPIB instrument on GPIB board 0, at primary address 5, and no secondary addressing.
789632 INSTR{GPIB::5}"

789664 no error
789673 ERROR
789680 (ABC) 
789687 The name of the VI that is calling this VI.  If an error occurs during the operation of this VI, the value in source will be placed in the source element of the error out cluster. 
789870 (I32) 
789877 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
790128 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
790386      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
790437      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
790484      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
790542      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
790599      error, and a positive value is a warning.
790647      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
790694      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
790743 ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing."

955120 Wrequested byte count specifies the number of characters to be read. If you want to read all of the characters currently at the serial port, first execute the Bytes at Serial Port VI to determine the exact number of bytes ready to be read. 987973 error out is a cluster that describes the error status after this VI executes. If an error occurred before this VI was called, error out is the same as error in. 1043926 |error in is a cluster that describes the error status before this VI executes. If error in indicates that an error occurred before this VI was called, this VI may choose not to execute its function, but just pass the error through to its error out cluster. If no error has occurred, then this VI executes normally and sets its own error status in error out. Use the error handler VIs to look up the error code and to display the corresponding error message. Using error in and error out clusters is a convenient way to check errors and to specify execution order by wiring the error output from one subVI to the error input of the next.
1044565 status is TRUE if an error occurred before this VI was called, or FALSE if not. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code."

1105160 This vi handles the RS-232 communications for a UUT. FC In and FC Out are used for flow control.
1105257 Mode 0 - Write then Read.
1105283 Mode 1 - Write only.
1105304 Mode 2 - Read only.
1105324 Timeout is in seconds.

1261222 84(u32) task ID: identifies the group and I/O pattern.D@(u32) pattern: specifies the new state of the lines in the port.
1261345 x(i32) line mask: determines which lines in the port the write affects. If you set line mask to -1, the VI writes to the entire port and sets all the lines in the port to the states specified by the bits in pattern. If you set only bit n in line mask, the VI changes only line n in the port to the state that bit n of pattern specifies. The default setting for line mask is -1.51(u32) task ID out: has the same value as task ID.
1261777 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
1262122      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
1262174      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
1262232      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
1262290      error, and a positive value is a warning.
1262338      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
1262388      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
1262437 1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred."

1288237 (i32) line mask: determines which lines this VI reads. If you set line mask to -1 (all ones), the VI reads the entire port. If you set only bit n in line mask, the VI reads only line n of the port. If the state of line n is high, the VI sets bit n of pattern. The VI sets to 0 the bits of pattern that correspond to lines the VI has not read. The default setting for line mask is -1 which is shown as all ones since the binary representation is the default selection.62(u32) pattern: the data the VI read from the port.51(u32) task ID out: has the same value as task ID.

1316720 (gc(i16) device: the device number you assigned to the data acquisition device when you configured it.
1316825 /(i16) port width: the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4-bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8.
1316990 When port width is greater than the physical port width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port  number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5.
1317388 ?(i32) line direction map: specifies the direction of each line in the port. If a bit is 0 in the line map, the line is an input line. If a bit is 1, the line is an output line. Setting line direction map to -1 makes all the lines in a port output lines. Setting line direction map to 0 makes all the lines in a port input lines. Except for the NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10, this is how you must use line direction map. The NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10 are the only boards on which you can configure lines within a port for different directions. The default for line direction map is 0.
1317966 (u32) task ID: uniquely identifies the group. You use this value as the task ID to refer to this group in subsequent digital port VI calls.
1318109 (cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
1318309      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
1318361      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
1318419      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
1318477      error, and a positive value is a warning.
1318525      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
1318575      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
1318624 xt(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. Regardless of the value of status, this VI clears the input operation.
1318745 D(string) port number: specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use an SCXI-1160, SCXI-1161, SCXI-1162, or SCXI-1163 module, use the SCx!MDy syntax, where x is the chassis and y is the module device number, to specify the module."

1319344 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information. 1364939 HDcode out is the error code indicated by the error in or error code.
1365012 no error
1365021 ERROR
1365027 no error
1365036 ERROR
1365044 =type of dialog determines what type dialog box will be displayed, if any. Regardless of its value, the VI outputs error information and message describing the error.
1365215 displays no dialog box. This is useful if you want to have programmatic control over how the error is handled.
1365330 (the default value) displays a dialog box with a single OK button. After the user responds, the VI returns control to the main VI.
1365465 displays a dialog box with buttons allowing the user to either continue or stop. If the user cancels, the VI calls the Stop function to halt execution. 
1365621 no dialog
1365631 OK message
1365642 continue or stop message
1365670 exception action is a way for you to create exceptions to error handling. You can treat what is normally an error as no error, or treat a no error condition as an error using this parameter. 
1365866 (the default value) performs no error exception handling. 
1365929 cancels error under the following conditions:
1365977 If the VI detects an error, as described in the status and error code parameters, and if that error code value matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to FALSE, code out to 0, and source out to an empty string. An empty exception source string matches any error source string.
1366317 sets error under the following conditions:
1366362 If the VI detects no error, as described in the status and error code parameters, but the code value of error in matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to TRUE, code out to the code value from error in, and source out to the source value from error in.
1366675 b^exception code is the error code that you want to treat as an exception. By default, it is 0.
1366773 error code is a numeric error code. If error in indicates an error, the VI ignores error code. If not, the VI tests it. A non-zero value signifies an error.
1366932 no exception
1366946 cancel error on match
1366968 set error on match
1366988 user-defined codes is an array of the numeric error codes you define in your VIs. The VI searches this array after searching the internal list of error codes. Codes in the range of 5000 to 9999 are reserved for users.
1367208 user-defined descriptions is an array of descriptions of user-defined codes. If an incoming error matches one in user-defined codes, the VI uses the corresponding description from user-defined descriptions in message.
1367426 2.source out indicates the source of the error.
1367474 }yexception source is the error message that you want to use to test for an exception. By default, it is an empty string. 
1367599 error source is an optional string you can use to describe the source of error code. The VI uses the string in message if there is an error.
1367740 jferror in describes an error that you want to check. If unwired, this VI checks error code for errors.
1367846 status is TRUE if an error occurred. If this value is FALSE, then the error handler assumes that no error occurred according to the error in, and then checks the error code.
1368023 no error
1368032 ERROR
1368038 no error
1368047 ERROR51code is the error code associated with an error.
1368105 source. In case of an error, most VIs that use the error in and error out clusters set source to the name of the VI or function that produced the error.
1368258 |xerror out contains the same information as status out, code out, and source out. It has the same structure as error in.
1368382 status is TRUE if an error occurred. If this value is FALSE, then the error handler assumes that no error occurred according to the error in, and then checks the error code.
1368559 no error
1368568 ERROR
1368574 no error
1368583 ERROR51code is the error code associated with an error.
1368641 source. In case of an error, most VIs that use the error in and error out clusters set source to the name of the VI or function that produced the error.
1368794 mimessage describes the error code that occurred, the source of the error, and a description of the error.

1417768 error codes (hidden)
1418099 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.

1420276 . Interpret it bit-wise as follows: x4000: serial port VI error; x0001: receiving queue overflowed or character was received after end-of-file character; x0002: character was lost by overwrite; x0004: parity error; x0008: framing error; x0010: break condition; x0020: CTS timeout; x0040:  DSR timeout; x0080: RLSD timeout; x0100: transmission queue was full when new character arrived; x0200: parallel device timeout; x0400: parallel device I/O error; x0800: parallel device not selected; x1000: parallel device out of paper; x8000: requested mode is  not supported or the idComDev parameter is invalid.  Consult the LabVIEW serial port manual for more information.SD
1420960 message
1421083  INSTRUCTIONS:
1421099 Normal Use:  When using subVIs that incorporate the error in/error out (or error I/O) structure, place this handler where you want to inform the user of an error, typically at the end of the I/O data path, as the last action of the program.  If the error in status is ERROR, the handler creates a message describing the error and its source.  If the type of dialog = 1 (default), the message is displayed to the user, who can only acknowedge it.  If the type = 2, the user can acknowledge the message or abort execution; aborting a program with active I/O is not recommended.  If the type = 0, no message is displayed; this is used to process the error programmatically, and the error out cluster elements are wired to individual terminals for that reason.  
1421859 Other Uses:
1421873 local testing.  To test the error code of a subVI or function that does not have the error I/O structure, you can wire its error code and a source string to the local error code and error source inputs.  If error in status indicates no error and error code is not equal to 0, the local code and source are substituted for the error in values, and the status is set TRUE (ERROR).
1422253 user-defined codes.  The error handler has tables of error codes and descriptions for all LabVIEW I/O operations (file, GPIB, DAQ, etc.).  You can augment the tables with the user-defined arrays.  Codes from 5000 to 9999 are reserved for user assignments.
1422510 exception handling.  This mechanism is available either to set the error out status FALSE on what is normally an error or to set the status TRUE on what is normally not an error.  If exception action > 0, the error in code and source are checked.  If they match the exception code and source, the error out status is adjusted accordingly.  That is, if the action = 1, the error out status is set to FALSE and code is set to zero and if the action = 2, the error out is set to TRUE and the code is unchanged.  An empty exception source matches any error in source.  H

1467693  INSTRUCTIONS:
1467709 Normal Use:  When using subVIs that incorporate the error in/error out (or error I/O) structure, place this handler where you want to inform the user of an error, typically at the end of the I/O data path, as the last action of the program.  If the error in status is ERROR, the handler creates a message describing the error and its source.  If the type of dialog = 1 (default), the message is displayed to the user, who can only acknowedge it.  If the type = 2, the user can acknowledge the message or abort execution; aborting a program with active I/O is not recommended.  If the type = 0, no message is displayed; this is used to process the error programmatically, and the error out cluster elements are wired to individual terminals for that reason.  
1468469 Other Uses:
1468483 local testing.  To test the error code of a subVI or function that does not have the error I/O structure, you can wire its error code and a source string to the local error code and error source inputs.  If error in status indicates no error and error code is not equal to 0, the local code and source are substituted for the error in values, and the status is set TRUE (ERROR).
1468863 user-defined codes.  The error handler has tables of error codes and descriptions for all LabVIEW I/O operations (file, GPIB, DAQ, etc.).  You can augment the tables with the user-defined arrays.  Codes from 5000 to 9999 are reserved for user assignments.
1469120 exception handling.  This mechanism is available either to set the error out status FALSE on what is normally an error or to set the status TRUE on what is normally not an error.  If exception action > 0, the error in code and source are checked.  If they match the exception code and source, the error out status is adjusted accordingly.  That is, if the action = 1, the error out status is set to FALSE and code is set to zero and if the action = 2, the error out is set to TRUE and the code is unchanged.  An empty exception source matches any error in source.  
1469687 . Interpret it bit-wise as follows: x4000: serial port VI error; x0001: receiving queue overflowed or character was received after end-of-file character; x0002: character was lost by overwrite; x0004: parity error; x0008: framing error; x0010: break condition; x0020: CTS timeout; x0040:  DSR timeout; x0080: RLSD timeout; x0100: transmission queue was full when new character arrived; x0200: parallel device timeout; x0400: parallel device I/O error; x0800: parallel device not selected; x1000: parallel device out of paper; x8000: requested mode is  not supported or the idComDev parameter is invalid.  Consult the LabVIEW serial port manual for more information.

1474304 General Error Handler.vi
1474335 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.

1480306 ,yudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
1480429 &port width is the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
1480589 When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
1480982 (U32) pattern: contains the binary data to write to the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit for the port specified by the port number control. 
1481136 M(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for output and then writes the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply writes the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
1481473 )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.

1506475 dyudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
1506598 =port width is the total width in bits or the number of lines of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
1506781 When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
1507174 (U32) pattern: contains the binary data read from the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit from the port specified by the port number control. 
1507327 J(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for input and then reads the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply reads the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
1507661 )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.

1526488 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
1526667 The Read from Digital Port VI reads a user configured digital port.  The reading is displayed as a binary number in [pattern].
1526795 You have the option to not reconfigure the port as an input port by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value. You can also concatenate multiple ports to operate as one large port by using the port width paramter.
1527018 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8.
1527153 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Read for more information.
